      <table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;width: 22em;">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
          <img alt="[]" data-file-height="100" data-file-width="75" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/30px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/45px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/60px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 2x" width="30"/>
         </a>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;">
         <b>
          This article contains
          <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
           IPA
          </a>
          phonetic symbols.
         </b>
         Without proper
         <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet#Fonts" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
          rendering support
         </a>
         , you may see
         <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">
          question marks, boxes, or other symbols
         </a>
         instead of
         <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">
          Unicode
         </a>
         characters. For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          Help:IPA
         </a>
         .
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <b>
        Spanish orthography
       </b>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Orthography" title="Orthography">
        orthography
       </a>
       used in the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish language
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Alphabet" title="Alphabet">
        alphabet
       </a>
       uses the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">
        Latin script
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Spelling" title="Spelling">
        spelling
       </a>
       is fairly
       <a href="/wiki/Phonemic_orthography" title="Phonemic orthography">
        phonemic
       </a>
       , especially in comparison to more opaque orthographies like
       <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">
        English
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">
        Irish
       </a>
       , having a relatively consistent mapping of
       <a href="/wiki/Grapheme" title="Grapheme">
        graphemes
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">
        phonemes
       </a>
       ; in other words, the pronunciation of a given Spanish-language word can largely be predicted from its spelling and to a slightly lesser extent vice-versa. Notable features of Spanish
       <a href="/wiki/Punctuation" title="Punctuation">
        punctuation
       </a>
       include the lack of the
       <a href="/wiki/Serial_comma" title="Serial comma">
        serial comma
       </a>
       and the inverted question marks and exclamation points: ¿ ¡.
      </p>
      <p>
       Spanish uses capital letters much less often than English; they are not used on adjectives derived from proper nouns (e.g.
       <i>
        francés
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        español
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        israelí
       </i>
       from
       <i>
        Francia
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        España
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        Israel
       </i>
       , respectively) and book titles capitalize only the first word (e.g.
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Revolt_of_the_Masses" title="The Revolt of the Masses">
         La rebelión de las masas
        </a>
       </i>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       Spanish uses only the acute accent, over any vowel: á é í ó ú. This accent is used to mark the tonic (
       <a href="/wiki/Stress_(linguistics)" title="Stress (linguistics)">
        stressed
       </a>
       ) syllable, though it may also be used occasionally in monosyllabic words to distinguish homophones such as
       <i>
        si
       </i>
       ('if') and
       <i>
        sí
       </i>
       ('yes'). The only other
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diacritics" title="Diacritics">
        diacritics
       </a>
       used are the tilde on the letter ⟨ñ⟩, which is considered a separate letter from ⟨n⟩, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Diaeresis_(diacritic)" title="Diaeresis (diacritic)">
        diaeresis
       </a>
       used in some instances over ⟨u⟩ in words like
       <i>
        bilingüe
       </i>
       ('bilingual').
      </p>
      <p>
       In contrast with English, Spanish has an official body that governs linguistic rules, orthography among them: the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Spanish_Academy" title="Royal Spanish Academy">
        Royal Spanish Academy
       </a>
       , which makes periodic changes to orthography. It is the policy of the Royal Spanish Academy that, when quoting older texts, one should update spelling to the current rules, except in discussions of the history of the Spanish language.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

         </a>
         <ul>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Alphabet_in_Spanish">
        Alphabet in Spanish
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_orthography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Alphabet in Spanish">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The Spanish language is written using the Spanish alphabet, which is the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">
        Latin script
       </a>
       with one additional letter:
       <i>
        eñe
       </i>
       "
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%91" title="Ñ">
        ñ
       </a>
       ", for a total of 27 letters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nuevaortografia2010_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nuevaortografia2010-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although the letters "k" and "w" are part of the alphabet, they appear only in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loanwords" title="Loanwords">
        loanwords
       </a>
       such as
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/karate#Spanish" title="wikt:karate">
          karate
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/kilo#Spanish" title="wikt:kilo">
          kilo
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/waterpolo#Spanish" title="wikt:waterpolo">
          waterpolo
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/wolframio#Spanish" title="wikt:wolframio">
          wolframio
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       (tungsten). Each letter has a single official name according to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Academia_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Real Academia Española">
        Real Academia Española
       </a>
       's new 2010 Common Orthography,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but in some regions alternative traditional names coexist as explained below. The digraphs "ch" and "ll" were considered letters of the alphabet from 1754 to 2010 (and sorted separately from "c" and "l" from 1803 to 1994).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The digraph "rr" is occasionally considered a letter, but officially it was never so.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center; min-width:60%; margin-left:5px">
       <caption>
        Spanish alphabet
       </caption>

         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">

         <sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_c,z">

         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          silent
         </small>
         <sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_h">

          </a>

        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /i/
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_ch">
        <b>
         <a href="#ref_ch">
          ^1
         </a>
        </b>
       </span>
       The sequence ⟨ch⟩ represents the affricate
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /tʃ/
       </span>
       . The digraph was formerly treated as a single letter, called
       <i>
        che
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_c,z">
        <b>
         <a href="#ref_c,z">
          ^2
         </a>
        </b>
       </span>
       The phonemes
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /θ/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       have merged in many dialects; see
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seseo" title="Seseo">
         seseo
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_h">
        <b>
         <a href="#ref_h">
          ^3
         </a>
        </b>
       </span>
       With the exception of some loanwords:
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/h%C3%A1mster#Spanish" title="wikt:hámster">
          hámster
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/hach%C3%ADs#Spanish" title="wikt:hachís">
          hachís
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/hawaiano#Spanish" title="wikt:hawaiano">
          hawaiano
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , which have
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /x/
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center; min-width:60%; margin-left:5px">

      <p>
       <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_l">
        <b>
         <a href="#ref_l">
          ^4
         </a>
        </b>
       </span>
       When ⟨l⟩ is written double (e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/calle#Spanish" title="wikt:calle">
          calle
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ), it represents the
       <a href="/wiki/Palatal_lateral_approximant" title="Palatal lateral approximant">
        palatal lateral
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʎ/
       </span>
       in a few dialects; but in most dialects—because of the historical merger called
       <a href="/wiki/Ye%C3%ADsmo" title="Yeísmo">
        yeísmo
       </a>
       —it, like the letter ⟨y⟩, represents the phoneme
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʝ/
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_q">
        <b>
         <a href="#ref_q">
          ^5
         </a>
        </b>
       </span>
       Used only in the digraph ⟨qu⟩.
      </p>

        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ʝ/
         </span>
         ,
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /i/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /θ/
         </span>
         <sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_c,z">
          <a href="#endnote_c,z">
           2
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_r">
        <b>
         <a href="#ref_r">
          ^6
         </a>
        </b>
       </span>
       The digraph ⟨rr⟩, which only appears between vowels, represents the trill
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [r]
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       For details on Spanish pronunciation, see
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_phonology" title="Spanish phonology">
        Spanish phonology
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">
        Help:IPA/Spanish
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       When
       <a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">
        acute accent
       </a>
       and diaeresis marks are used on vowels (⟨á⟩, ⟨é⟩, ⟨í⟩, ⟨ó⟩, ⟨ú⟩ and ⟨ü⟩) they are considered variants of the plain vowel letters, but ⟨ñ⟩ is considered a separate letter from ⟨n⟩. This makes a difference when sorting alphabetically: ⟨ñ⟩ appears in dictionaries after ⟨n⟩. For example, in a Spanish dictionary
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pi%C3%B1ata#Spanish" title="wikt:piñata">
          piñata
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       comes after
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pinza#Spanish" title="wikt:pinza">
          pinza
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       There are five
       <a href="/wiki/Digraph_(orthography)" title="Digraph (orthography)">
        digraphs
       </a>
       : ⟨
       <a href="/wiki/Ch_(digraph)" title="Ch (digraph)">
        ch
       </a>
       ⟩ ("che" or "ce hache"), ⟨
       <a href="/wiki/Ll" title="Ll">
        ll
       </a>
       ⟩ ("elle" or "doble ele"), ⟨
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rr_(digraph)" title="Rr (digraph)">
        rr
       </a>
       ⟩ ("doble erre"), ⟨
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gu_(digraph)" title="Gu (digraph)">
        gu
       </a>
       ⟩ ("ge u") and ⟨
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qu_(digraph)" title="Qu (digraph)">
        qu
       </a>
       ⟩ ("cu u").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While
       <i>
        che
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        elle
       </i>
       were formerly treated each as a single letter,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nuevaortografia2010_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-nuevaortografia2010-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in 1994 the tenth congress of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_of_Spanish_Language_Academies" title="Association of Spanish Language Academies">
        Association of Spanish Language Academies
       </a>
       , by request of
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       and other international organizations, agreed to
       <a href="/wiki/Collation" title="Collation">
        alphabetize
       </a>
       ⟨ch⟩ and ⟨ll⟩ as ordinary sequences of letters. Thus, for example, in dictionaries,
       <i>
        chico
       </i>
       is alphabetized after
       <i>
        centro
       </i>
       and before
       <i>
        ciudad
       </i>
       , instead of being alphabetized after all words beginning with
       <i>
        cu-
       </i>
       as was formerly done.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Despite their former status as unitary letters of the alphabet, ⟨ch⟩ and ⟨ll⟩ have always been treated as sequences with regard to the rules of capitalization. Thus the word
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/chill%C3%B3n#Spanish" title="wikt:chillón">
          chillón
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       in a text written in all caps is
       <i>
        CHILLÓN
       </i>
       , not *
       <i>
        ChILlÓN
       </i>
       , and if it is the first word of a sentence, it is written
       <i>
        Chillón
       </i>
       , not *
       <i>
        CHillón
       </i>
       . Sometimes, one finds
       <a href="/wiki/Elevator" title="Elevator">
        lifts
       </a>
       with buttons marked
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/LLamar#Spanish" title="wikt:LLamar">
          LLamar
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , but this double capitalization has always been incorrect according to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Academia_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Real Academia Española">
        RAE
       </a>
       rules.
      </p>
      <p>
       In Spanish text, the letters are ranked from most to least common: ⟨E A O S R N I D L C T U M P B G V Y Q H F Z J Ñ X W K⟩,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the vowels take around 45% of the text.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_names">
        Alternative names
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_orthography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Alternative names">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        B and V
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nuevaortografia2010_1-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-nuevaortografia2010-1">
          [1]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dt>
       <dd>
        The letters ⟨b⟩ and ⟨v⟩ were originally simply known as
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/be#Spanish" title="wikt:be">
           be
          </a>
         </span>
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ve#Spanish" title="wikt:ve">
           ve
          </a>
         </span>
        </i>
        , which in modern Spanish are pronounced identically. In
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Spanish" title="Old Spanish">
         Old Spanish
        </a>
        , they likely represented different sounds but the sounds merged later. Their usual names are
        <i>
         be
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         uve
        </i>
        ;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
         <a href="#cite_note-7">
          [7]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
         <a href="#cite_note-8">
          [8]
         </a>
        </sup>
        in some regions, speakers may instead add something to the names to distinguish them. Some
        <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Spanish" title="Mexican Spanish">
         Mexicans
        </a>
        and most
        <a href="/wiki/Peruvian_Spanish" title="Peruvian Spanish">
         Peruvians
        </a>
        generally say
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          be
         </span>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/grande#Spanish" title="wikt:grande">
           grande
          </a>
         </span>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/chica#Spanish" title="wikt:chica">
           chica
          </a>
         </span>
        </i>
        ('big B' / 'little V');
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Argentine_Spanish" title="Argentine Spanish">
         Argentines
        </a>
        , Uruguayans and Chileans,
        <i>
         be
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/larga#Spanish" title="wikt:larga">
           larga
          </a>
         </span>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/corta#Spanish" title="wikt:corta">
           corta
          </a>
         </span>
        </i>
        ('long B' / 'short V'). Some people give examples of words spelt with the letter; e.g.,
        <i>
         b de
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/burro#Spanish" title="wikt:burro">
           burro
          </a>
         </span>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         v de
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/vaca#Spanish" title="wikt:vaca">
           vaca
          </a>
         </span>
        </i>
        ('b as in
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/burro#Spanish" title="wikt:burro">
           burro
          </a>
         </span>
        </i>
        ' / 'v as in
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/vaca#Spanish" title="wikt:vaca">
           vaca
          </a>
         </span>
        </i>
        ');
        <a href="/wiki/Colombian_Spanish" title="Colombian Spanish">
         Colombians
        </a>
        tend to say
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          be grande
         </span>
        </i>
        for B and
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          ve
         </span>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/peque%C3%B1a#Spanish" title="wikt:pequeña">
           pequeña
          </a>
         </span>
        </i>
        for V. In Venezuela, they called B as
        <i>
         b de
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Bol%C3%ADvar#Spanish" title="wikt:Bolívar">
           Bolívar
          </a>
         </span>
         , and V as
        </i>
        v de
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Venezuela#Spanish" title="wikt:Venezuela">
           Venezuela
          </a>
         </span>
        </i>
        ; but also, as
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          be alta
         </span>
         y
        </i>
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          ve baja
         </span>
        </i>
        ('tall B' / 'short V'). Regardless of these regional differences, all Spanish-speaking people recognize
        <i>
         be
        </i>
        as the official name of B.
       </dd>
       <dt>
        R
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nuevaortografia2010_1-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-nuevaortografia2010-1">
          [1]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dt>
       <dd>
        The digraph ⟨
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rr_(digraph)" title="Rr (digraph)">
         rr
        </a>
        ⟩ is sometimes called
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          doble erre
         </span>
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          erre doble
         </span>
        </i>
        . It is sometimes suggested that the name of the letter ⟨r⟩ be
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          ere
         </span>
        </i>
        when it is single, and
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          erre
         </span>
        </i>
        when it is double, but the dictionary of the Real Academia Española defines the name of ⟨r⟩ as
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          erre
         </span>
        </i>
        .
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          Ere
         </span>
        </i>
        is considered obsolete.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
         <a href="#cite_note-9">
          [9]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The name
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          ere
         </span>
        </i>
        was used when referring specifically to the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_tap" title="Alveolar tap">
         alveolar tap
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɾ/
        </span>
        and
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          erre
         </span>
        </i>
        referring to the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_trill" title="Alveolar trill">
         alveolar trill
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /r/
        </span>
        . The two contrast between vowels, with the latter being represented with ⟨rr⟩, but the sounds are otherwise in
        <a href="/wiki/Complementary_distribution" title="Complementary distribution">
         complementary distribution
        </a>
        so that a single ⟨r⟩ may represent either. As a referent to the trill sound rather than the phoneme,
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          erre
         </span>
        </i>
        can refer to a single or double ⟨r⟩.
       </dd>
       <dt>
        W
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nuevaortografia2010_1-4">
         <a href="#cite_note-nuevaortografia2010-1">
          [1]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dt>
       <dd>
        In
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_American_Spanish" title="Latin American Spanish">
         Latin American Spanish
        </a>
        , ⟨w⟩ is sometimes called
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          doble ve
         </span>
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          ve doble
         </span>
        </i>
        , or
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          doble uve
         </span>
        </i>
        . In Colombia and Mexico, because of English acculturation, the letter is usually called
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          doble u
         </span>
        </i>
        (like English "double u"). In Spain it is usually called
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          uve doble
         </span>
        </i>
        .
       </dd>
       <dt>
        I
       </dt>
       <dd>
        Because of its origin, ⟨i⟩ is occasionally known as
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          i latina
         </span>
        </i>
        ("Latin i") to distinguish it from ⟨y⟩, which is known as
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          i griega
         </span>
        </i>
        ("Greek i").
       </dd>
       <dt>
        Y
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nuevaortografia2010_1-5">
         <a href="#cite_note-nuevaortografia2010-1">
          [1]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dt>
       <dd>
        The most common name for ⟨y⟩ in Spain is
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          i griega
         </span>
        </i>
        , but in Latin American Spanish it has been commonly superseded by
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          ye
         </span>
        </i>
        , in an effort to standardize on a one-word name, as opposed to a name consisting of two words. Using
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          ye
         </span>
        </i>
        as the only name for the letter is one of the newest proposed changes specified by the 2010 new common orthography.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nuevaortografia2010_1-6">
         <a href="#cite_note-nuevaortografia2010-1">
          [1]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
       <dt>
        Z
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nuevaortografia2010_1-7">
         <a href="#cite_note-nuevaortografia2010-1">
          [1]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dt>
       <dd>
        The name for ⟨z⟩ is
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          zeta
         </span>
        </i>
        (formerly
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          ceta
         </span>
        </i>
        , pronounced the same).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
         <a href="#cite_note-10">
          [10]
         </a>
        </sup>
        In older Spanish, it was called
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          zeda
         </span>
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          ceda
         </span>
        </i>
        , and the diminutive form of this word,
        <a href="/wiki/Cedilla" title="Cedilla">
         cedilla
        </a>
        , is now used in both Spanish and English to refer to the diacritic mark exhibited in the letter ⟨ç⟩.
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Orthography">
        Orthography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_orthography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Orthography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Spanish orthography is such that the pronunciation of most words is unambiguous given their written form; the main exception is the letter ⟨x⟩, which usually represents
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ks/
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       , but can also represent
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /x/
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʃ/
       </span>
       , especially in proper nouns from times of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Spanish" title="Old Spanish">
        Old Spanish
       </a>
       , as in
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toponymy_of_Mexico" title="Toponymy of Mexico">
          <i>
           México
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Xim%C3%A9nez" title="Pedro Ximénez">
        Pedro Ximénez
       </a>
       (both
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /x/
       </span>
       ). These orthographic rules are similar to, but not the same as, those of other
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
        Iberian Peninsula
       </a>
       , such as
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The converse does not always hold, i.e. for a given pronunciation there may be multiple possible spellings. The main issues are:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        the use of both ⟨b⟩ and ⟨v⟩ for
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /b/
        </span>
        ;
       </li>
       <li>
        the use of both ⟨j⟩ and ⟨g⟩ for
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /x/
        </span>
        before ⟨e⟩ and ⟨i⟩;
       </li>
       <li>
        the silent ⟨h⟩;
       </li>
       <li>
        for the speakers who have merged
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʝ/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʎ/
        </span>
        , the various use of ⟨y⟩, ⟨ll⟩ or ⟨hi⟩ in different words;
       </li>
       <li>
        the use of ⟨hu⟩, ⟨gu⟩ or ⟨bu⟩ before a vowel for
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /w/
        </span>
        (although many speakers distinguish some or all of these combinations);
       </li>
       <li>
        for speakers not in central and northern Spain, the use of ⟨c/z⟩ and ⟨s⟩ for
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /s/
        </span>
        ;
       </li>
       <li>
        the occasional use of accents to distinguish two words that sound the same, such as tú and tu, sí and si, más and mas.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <caption>
        Use of different letters for the same sound
       </caption>
       <tr>
        <th>
         sound
        </th>
        <th>
         before ⟨e/i⟩
        </th>
        <th>
         elsewhere
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr style="text-align:center;">
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /θ/ or /s/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         ⟨c⟩ (or ⟨z⟩ in some loanwords) or ⟨s⟩
        </td>
        <td>
         ⟨z⟩ or ⟨s⟩
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="text-align:center;">

         </span>

        <td>

         <i>

         <a href="/wiki/Paisa" title="Paisa">
          Paisa
         </a>
         region of Colombia, and Andes, this sound is made with the tip of the tongue rather than the blade, with a sound quality intermediate between the alveolar
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [s]
         </span>

         <i>
          <b>
           s
          </b>
          ea
         </i>
         and the palato-alveolar
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ʃ]
         </span>
         of
         <i>
          <b>
           s
          </b>
          he
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>

      <ol>
       <li>
        <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_1">
         <b>
          <a href="#ref_1">
           ^
          </a>
         </b>
        </span>
        Orthographic &lt;w&gt; in names of Visigothic origin is thought to have been pronounced [
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         β
        </span>
        ] in Old Spanish (in which /b/ and /
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         β
        </span>
        / are separate phonemes); /
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         β
        </span>
        / is also spelled &lt;v&gt; in Old Spanish. See
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Spanish#Merger_of_/b/_and_/v/" title="History of Spanish">
         History of Spanish#Merger of /b/ and /v/
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       The only consonant letters that can be doubled in the Spanish orthography are "l", "r" (as the digraphs "ll" and "rr"), "c" (only when the two "c"s have different sounds:
       <i>
        acción, diccionario
       </i>
       ), "n" (e.g.
       <i>
        innato, perenne, connotar, dígannos
       </i>
       ), and "b" (in a few words with the prefix
       <i>
        sub-
       </i>
       :
       <i>
        subbase, subbético
       </i>
       ). Exceptions are
       <i>
        gamma
       </i>
       (and its derivatives
       <i>
        gammaglobulina, gammagrafía
       </i>
       ),
       <i>
        digamma, kappa, atto-
       </i>
       , as well as unadapted foreign words (including proper names) and their derivations (see below).
      </p>

            </b>
            s
            <b>
             o
            </b>
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         between
         <i>
          c
          <b>
           oa
          </b>
          t
         </i>
         (American more than British) and
         <i>

        </td>
