      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_letter_Y">
        The letter Y
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_orthography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: The letter Y">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The letter "y" is consistently used in the consonantal value. The use of the letter "y" for a vowel or a semivowel is very restricted. The diphthongs
       <i>
        ai, ei, oi, ui
       </i>
       are usually written
       <i>
        ay, ey, oy, uy
       </i>
       at the end of words (e. g.
       <i>
        hay, ley, voy, muy
       </i>
       ), though exceptions may occur in loanwords (e.g.
       <i>
        bonsái, agnusdéi
       </i>
       ). The letter
       <i>
        y
       </i>
       is conserved in rarely used encliticized verbal forms like
       <i>
        doyte, haylas
       </i>
       (it is more normal to say
       <i>
        te doy, las hay
       </i>
       ). The letter "y" is used for the vowel
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /i/
       </span>
       in the conjunction
       <i>
        y
       </i>
       and in some acronyms, like
       <i>
        pyme
       </i>
       (from
       <i>
        pequeña y mediana empresa
       </i>
       ). Otherwise, "y" for a vowel or semivowel occurs only in some archaically-spelled proper names and their derivations:
       <i>
        Guaymas, guaymeño
       </i>
       , and also
       <i>
        fraybentino
       </i>
       (from
       <i>
        Fray Bentos
       </i>
       with regular usage of "y" in a word-final diphthong). Derivatives of foreign proper names also conserve "y":
       <i>
        taylorismo
       </i>
       , from
       <i>
        Taylor
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Special_and_modified_letters">
        Special and modified letters
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_orthography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Special and modified letters">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The vowels can be marked with an
       <a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">
        acute accent
       </a>
       —á, é, í, ó, ú, ý—for two purposes: to mark
       <a href="/wiki/Stress_(linguistics)" title="Stress (linguistics)">
        stress
       </a>
       if it does not follow the most common pattern, or to differentiate words that are otherwise spelled identically (called the
       <i>
        tilde diacrítica
       </i>
       in Spanish). The accented "y" is found only in some proper names:
       <i>
        Aýna, Laýna, Ýñiguez
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       A silent "u" is used between "g" and "e" or "i" to indicate a hard "g" pronunciation, so that "gue" represents
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɡe/
       </span>
       and "gui" represents
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɡi/
       </span>
       . The letter "
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%9C" title="Ü">
        ü
       </a>
       " ("u" with diaeresis,) is used in this context to indicate that the "u" is not silent, e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ping%C3%BCino#Spanish" title="wikt:pingüino">
          pingüino
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       /pinˈgwino/. The diaeresis may occur also in Spanish poetry, occasionally, over either vowel of a diphthong, to indicate an irregular disyllabic pronunciation required by the meter (
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/v%C3%AFuda#Spanish" title="wikt:vïuda">
          vïuda
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , to be pronounced as three syllables). This is analogous to the use of "ï" in
       <i>
        naïve
       </i>
       in English.
      </p>
      <p>
       Also a silent "u" always follows a "q" when followed by "e" or "i", as in
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/queso#Spanish" title="wikt:queso">
          queso
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/qu%C3%ADmica#Spanish" title="wikt:química">
          química
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , but there is no case for the combination "qü", with "cu" fulfilling this role (as in
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cuesti%C3%B3n#Spanish" title="wikt:cuestión">
          cuestión
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ). There are no native words in Spanish with the combination "qua" nor "quo"; again, "cu" is used instead (
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cuando#Spanish" title="wikt:cuando">
          cuando
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ). When they appear, usually from Latin idioms such as
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/statu_quo#Spanish" title="wikt:statu quo">
          statu quo
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , the "u" is always pronounced, so "ü" is never needed after "q". Prior to the introduction of the 2010
       <i>
        Common Orthography
       </i>
       words such as
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cu%C3%B3rum#Spanish" title="wikt:cuórum">
          cuórum
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ('quorum'),
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cu%C3%A1sar#Spanish" title="wikt:cuásar">
          cuásar
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ('quasar') or
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Catar#Spanish" title="wikt:Catar">
          Catar
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ('Qatar') were spelled with "q"; this is no longer so.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Keyboard_requirements">
        Keyboard requirements
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_orthography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Keyboard requirements">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/QWERTY#Spanish" title="QWERTY">
        QWERTY § Spanish
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       To write Spanish on a
       <a href="/wiki/Typewriter" title="Typewriter">
        typewriter
       </a>
       or to set
       <a href="/wiki/Typeface" title="Typeface">
        type
       </a>
       , the special characters required are á, é, í, ó, ú, ñ, Ñ, ü, Ü, ¿, and ¡. Á, É, Í, Ó, and Ú are also prescribed by the RAE, although occasionally dispensed with in practice.
      </p>
      <p>
       As implemented on the mechanical typewriter, the keyboard contained a single
       <a href="/wiki/Dead_key" title="Dead key">
        dead key
       </a>
       , with the acute accent
       <span class="nowrap">
        ( ´ )
       </span>
       in the lower-case position, and the dieresis
       <span class="nowrap">
        ( ¨ )
       </span>
       in the upper-case position. With these, one could write á, é, í, ó, ú, and ü. A separate key provided ñ/Ñ. (A dead key ~ was not used on the Spanish keyboard, but was on the Portuguese.) ¿ and ¡ completed the required minimum. When an additional key was added to electro-mechanical typewriters, this was used for ª and º, though these are not required. (They are somewhat archaic
       <a href="/wiki/Ordinal_number_(linguistics)" title="Ordinal number (linguistics)">
        ordinal
       </a>
       abbreviations: 1º for
       <i>
        primero
       </i>
       , 2ª for
       <i>
        segunda
       </i>
       , etc.)
      </p>
      <p>
       As implemented in the
       <a href="/wiki/MS-DOS" title="MS-DOS">
        MS-DOS
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">
        operating system
       </a>
       and its successor
       <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">
        Microsoft Windows
       </a>
       , a ç/Ç pair, not required in Spanish but needed for Catalan, Portuguese, and French, is typically added, and the use of the acute accent and dieresis with capital letters (Á, É, Í, Ó, Ú, Ü) is supported. Although not needed for Spanish, another dead key with ` (the grave accent) in lower-case position and ^ (the circumflex accent) in upper-case position was included. · (the mid-line period, required in Catalan) is also found. To make room for these characters not on the standard English keyboard, characters used primarily in programming, science, and mathematics—[, ], {, }, /, \, |, &lt;, and &gt;—are removed, requiring special keystroke sequences to access.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Stress_and_accentuation">
        Stress and accentuation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_orthography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Stress and accentuation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Stress_in_Spanish" title="Stress in Spanish">
        Stress in Spanish
       </a>
       is marked unequivocally through a series of orthographic rules. The default stress is on the penultimate (next-to-last) syllable on words that end in a vowel, ⟨n⟩ or ⟨s⟩ and on the final syllable when the word ends in any consonant other than ⟨n⟩ or ⟨s⟩. Words that do not follow the default stress have an acute accent over the stressed vowel. The written accent will thus appear only in certain forms of a word and not others, for example
       <i>
        andén
       </i>
       , plural
       <i>
        andenes
       </i>
       . In many cases the accent is essential to understanding what a word means, for example hablo (I speak) as opposed to habló (he/she/Ud. spoke).
      </p>
      <p>
       For purposes of counting syllables and assigning stress in Spanish, where an unmarked high vowel is followed by another vowel the sequence is treated as a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rising_diphthong" title="Rising diphthong">
        rising diphthong
       </a>
       , counted as a single syllable—unlike Portuguese and Catalan, which tend to treat such a sequence as two syllables.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A syllable is of the form
       <i>
        XAXX
       </i>
       , where
       <i>
        X
       </i>
       represents a consonant, permissible consonant cluster, or no sound at all, and
       <i>
        A
       </i>
       represents a vowel, diphthong, or triphthong. A diphthong is any sequence of an unstressed
       <a href="/wiki/Close_vowel" title="Close vowel">
        high vowel
       </a>
       (⟨i⟩ or ⟨u⟩) with another vowel (as in
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/gracias#Spanish" title="wikt:gracias">
          <i>
           grac
           <b>
            ia
           </b>
           s
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/n%C3%A1utico#Spanish" title="wikt:náutico">
          <i>
           n
           <b>
            áu
           </b>
           tico
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ). And a triphthong is any combination of three vowels beginning and ending with unstressed high vowels (as in
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cambi%C3%A1is#Spanish" title="wikt:cambiáis">
          <i>
           camb
           <b>
            iái
           </b>
           s
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/buey#Spanish" title="wikt:buey">
          <i>
           b
           <b>
            uey
           </b>
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ). Hence Spanish writes
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/familia#Spanish" title="wikt:familia">
          familia
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       (no accent), while Portuguese and Catalan both put an accent mark on
       <i>
        <span lang="ca" xml:lang="ca">
         <i>
          <span lang="pt" xml:lang="pt">
           <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fam%C3%ADlia" title="wikt:família">
            família
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </span>
       </i>
       (all three languages stress the first ⟨i⟩). The letter ⟨h⟩ is not considered an interruption between vowels (so that
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ahumar#Spanish" title="wikt:ahumar">
          ahumar
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       is considered to have two syllables:
       <i>
        ahu-mar
       </i>
       ; this may vary in some regions, where ⟨h⟩ is used as a hiatus or diphthong-broking mark for unstressed vowels, so the pronunciation would be then
       <i>
        a-hu-mar
       </i>
       , though that trait is gradually disappearing).
      </p>
      <p>
       An accent over the
       <a href="/wiki/Close_vowel" title="Close vowel">
        high vowel
       </a>
       (⟨i⟩ or ⟨u⟩) of a vowel sequence prevents it from being a diphthong (i.e., it signals a
       <a href="/wiki/Hiatus_(linguistics)" title="Hiatus (linguistics)">
        hiatus
       </a>
       ): for example,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/t%C3%ADa#Spanish" title="wikt:tía">
          tía
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pa%C3%ADs#Spanish" title="wikt:país">
          país
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       have two syllables each.
      </p>
      <p>
       A word with final stress is called
       <a href="/wiki/Oxytone" title="Oxytone">
        oxytone
       </a>
       (or
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/aguda#Spanish" title="wikt:aguda">
          aguda
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       in traditional Spanish grammar texts); a word with penultimate stress is called
       <a href="/wiki/Paroxytone" title="Paroxytone">
        paroxytone
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/llana#Spanish" title="wikt:llana">
          llana
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/grave#Spanish" title="wikt:grave">
          grave
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ); a word with antepenultimate stress (stress on the third-to-last syllable) is called
       <a href="/wiki/Proparoxytone" title="Proparoxytone">
        proparoxytone
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/esdr%C3%BAjula#Spanish" title="wikt:esdrújula">
          esdrújula
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ). A word with preantepenultimate stress (on the fourth last syllable) or earlier does not have a common linguistic term in English, but in Spanish receives the name
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/sobresdr%C3%BAjula#Spanish" title="wikt:sobresdrújula">
          sobresdrújula
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       . (Spanish words can be stressed only on one of the last three syllables, except in the case of a verb form with
       <a href="/wiki/Clitic" title="Clitic">
        enclitic
       </a>
       pronouns, such as
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/poni%C3%A9ndoselo#Spanish" title="wikt:poniéndoselo">
          poniéndoselo
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       .) All proparoxytones and
       <i>
        sobresdrújulas
       </i>
       have a written accent mark.
      </p>
      <p>
       Adjectives spelled with a written accent (such as
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/f%C3%A1cil#Spanish" title="wikt:fácil">
          fácil
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/geogr%C3%A1fico#Spanish" title="wikt:geográfico">
          geográfico
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cort%C3%A9s#Spanish" title="wikt:cortés">
          cortés
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ) keep the written accent when they are made into adverbs with the
       <i>
        -mente
       </i>
       ending (thus
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/f%C3%A1cilmente#Spanish" title="wikt:fácilmente">
          fácilmente
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/geogr%C3%A1ficamente#Spanish" title="wikt:geográficamente">
          geográficamente
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cort%C3%A9smente#Spanish" title="wikt:cortésmente">
          cortésmente
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ), and do not gain any if they do not have one (thus
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/libremente#Spanish" title="wikt:libremente">
          libremente
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       from
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/libre#Spanish" title="wikt:libre">
          libre
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ). In the pronunciation of these adverbs—as with all adverbs in
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/-mente#Spanish" title="wikt:-mente">
          -mente
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       —primary stress is on the ending, on the
       <a href="/wiki/Ultima_(linguistics)" title="Ultima (linguistics)">
        penultimate syllable
       </a>
       . The original stress of the adjective—whether marked, as in
       <i>
        fácilmente
       </i>
       , or not marked, as in
       <i>
        libremente
       </i>
       —may be manifested as a secondary stress in the adverb.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Accentuation_of_capital_letters">
        Accentuation of capital letters
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_orthography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Accentuation of capital letters">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The Real Academia Española indicates that accents are required on capitals (but not when the capitals are used in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acronyms" title="Acronyms">
        acronyms
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Differential_accents">
        Differential accents
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_orthography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Differential accents">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_orthography.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Spanish_orthography.jpg/300px-Spanish_orthography.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Spanish_orthography.jpg/450px-Spanish_orthography.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Spanish_orthography.jpg/600px-Spanish_orthography.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_orthography.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Blackboard" title="Blackboard">
          Blackboard
         </a>
         used in a university classroom shows
         <a href="/wiki/Student" title="Student">
          students
         </a>
         ' efforts at placing "
         <a href="/wiki/%C3%9C" title="Ü">
          ü
         </a>
         " and
         <a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">
          acute accent
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">
          diacritic
         </a>
         used in Spanish orthography.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In a number of cases, homonyms are distinguished with written accents on the stressed (or only) syllable: for example,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/te#Spanish" title="wikt:te">
          te
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       (informal object case of 'you') vs.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/t%C3%A9#Spanish" title="wikt:té">
          té
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ('tea');
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/se#Spanish" title="wikt:se">
          se
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       (third person reflexive) vs.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/s%C3%A9#Spanish" title="wikt:sé">
          sé
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ('I know' or imperative 'be');
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/tu#Spanish" title="wikt:tu">
          tu
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       (informal 'your') vs.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/t%C3%BA#Spanish" title="wikt:tú">
          tú
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       (informal subject case of 'you'). When relative and interrogative pronouns have the same letters (as is often the case), the interrogative pronoun is accented and the relative pronoun is not:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          ¿A dónde vas?
         </span>
        </i>
        'Where are you going?'
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <i>
         <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
          A donde no puedas encontrarme.
         </span>
        </i>
        'Where you cannot find me.'
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The use of
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%C3%B3#Spanish" title="wikt:ó">
          ó
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       is poetic for the vocative:
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         ¡Ó señor!
        </span>
       </i>
       The use of ⟨ó⟩ for the word
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/o#Spanish" title="wikt:o">
          o
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       (meaning 'or') is a
       <a href="/wiki/Hypercorrection" title="Hypercorrection">
        hypercorrection
       </a>
       . Up until 2010, ⟨ó⟩ was used when applied to numbers:
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         7 ó 9
        </span>
       </i>
       ('7 or 9'), to avoid possible confusion with the digit 0. The tenth congress of the Association of Spanish Language Academies deemed the use of an accent unnecessary, as typewriting eliminates possible confusion due to the different shapes of ⟨0⟩ (zero) and ⟨o⟩ (the letter).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nuevaortografia2010_1-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-nuevaortografia2010-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       These diacritics are often called
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         acentos diacríticos
        </span>
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         tildes diacríticas
        </span>
       </i>
       in traditional Spanish grammar.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_words">
        Foreign words
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_orthography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Foreign words">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Loanwords in Spanish are usually written according to Spanish spelling conventions (
       <i>
        extranjerismos adaptados
       </i>
       ): e.g.,
       <i>
        pádel, fútbol, chófer, máster, cederrón
       </i>
       . However, some foreign words (
       <i>
        extranjerismos crudos
       </i>
       ) are used in Spanish texts in their original forms, not conform to Spanish orthographic conventions: e.g.,
       <i>
        ballet, blues, jazz, jeep, lady, pizza, sheriff, software
       </i>
       . RAE prescribes
       <i>
        extranjerismos crudos
       </i>
       to be written in italics in a text printed in roman type and vice versa, and in quotation marks in a manuscript text or when italics are not available:
      </p>
      <p>
       Quiero escuchar
       <i>
        jazz
       </i>
       y comer
       <i>
        pizza
       </i>
       .
       <i>
        Quiero escuchar
       </i>
       jazz
       <i>
        y comer
       </i>
       pizza. Quiero escuchar "jazz" y comer "pizza".
      </p>
      <p>
       In practice, this RAE prescription is not always followed.
      </p>
      <p>
       This typographical emphasis is not used for foreign proper names and their derivations; nor is it used for some Spanish derivations of
       <i>
        extranjerismos crudos
       </i>
       , such as
       <i>
        pizzería
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Capitalization">
        Capitalization
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_orthography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Capitalization">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Capitalization in Spanish is sparse compared to English. In general, only personal and place names, some abbreviations (e.g.
       <i>
        Sr. López
       </i>
       , but
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/se%C3%B1or#Spanish" title="wikt:señor">
          señor
         </a>
        </span>
        López
       </i>
       ); the first word (only) in the title of a book, movie, song, etc. (except when the title contains only two words, then the second word is also sometimes capitalized); and the first word in a sentence are capitalized, as are names of companies, government bodies, etc. Names of nationalities or languages are not capitalized, nor (in standard style) are days of the week and months of the year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Older_conventions">
        Older conventions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_orthography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Older conventions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Academia_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Real Academia Española">
        Spanish Royal Academy
       </a>
       has reformed the orthographic rules of Spanish many times.
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Spanish_language" title="Old Spanish language">
        Old Spanish
       </a>
       , ⟨x⟩ was used to represent the voiceless palatal sound
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʃ/
       </span>
       (as in
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dixo#Spanish" title="wikt:dixo">
          dixo
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       'he/she said'), while ⟨j⟩ represented the voiced palatal
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʒ/
       </span>
       (as in
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fijo#Spanish" title="wikt:fijo">
          fijo
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       'son'). With the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Spanish#Modern_development_of_the_Old_Spanish_sibilants" title="History of Spanish">
        changes of sibilants
       </a>
       in the 16th century, the two sounds merged as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʃ/
       </span>
       (later to become velar
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /x/
       </span>
       ), and the letter ⟨j⟩ was chosen for the single resulting phoneme in 1815. When
       <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes" title="Miguel de Cervantes">
        Cervantes
       </a>
       wrote
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Don_Quixote" title="Don Quixote">
         Don Quixote
        </a>
       </i>
       he spelled the name in the old way (and English preserves the ⟨x⟩), but modern editions in Spanish spell it with ⟨j⟩. For the use of ⟨x⟩ in Mexico—and in the name
       <i>
        México
       </i>
       itself—see below.
      </p>
      <p>
       The letter ⟨ç⟩ (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C-cedilla" title="C-cedilla">
        c-cedilla
       </a>
       )—which was first used in Old Spanish—is now obsolete in Spanish, having merged with ⟨z⟩ in a process similar to that of ⟨x⟩ and ⟨j⟩. Old Spanish
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cora%C3%A7on#Spanish" title="wikt:coraçon">
          coraçon
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cabe%C3%A7a#Spanish" title="wikt:cabeça">
          cabeça
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fuer%C3%A7a#Spanish" title="wikt:fuerça">
          fuerça
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       became modern
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/coraz%C3%B3n#Spanish" title="wikt:corazón">
          corazón
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cabeza#Spanish" title="wikt:cabeza">
          cabeza
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fuerza#Spanish" title="wikt:fuerza">
          fuerza
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Words formerly spelled with ⟨ze⟩ or ⟨zi⟩ (such as
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/catorze#Spanish" title="wikt:catorze">
          catorze
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dezir#Spanish" title="wikt:dezir">
          dezir
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/vezino#Spanish" title="wikt:vezino">
          vezino
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ) are now written with ⟨ce⟩ and ⟨ci⟩ (
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/catorce#Spanish" title="wikt:catorce">
          catorce
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/decir#Spanish" title="wikt:decir">
          decir
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/vecino#Spanish" title="wikt:vecino">
          vecino
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , respectively). The sequences ⟨ze⟩ and ⟨zi⟩ do not occur in modern Spanish except some loanwords:
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/zeugma#Spanish" title="wikt:zeugma">
          zeugma
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/zigurat#Spanish" title="wikt:zigurat">
          zigurat
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/zipizape#Spanish" title="wikt:zipizape">
          zipizape
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ; some borrowed words have double spellings:
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/zinc#Spanish" title="wikt:zinc">
          zinc
         </a>
        </span>
        /
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cinc#Spanish" title="wikt:cinc">
          cinc
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The old spellings with ⟨ç⟩, ⟨ze⟩, and ⟨zi⟩ remained in use until the eighteenth century. They were replaced by ⟨z⟩, ⟨ce⟩, and ⟨ci⟩, respectively in 1726.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ort1726_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ort1726-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ⟨Ze⟩ and ⟨zi⟩ continued to be used in some words due to their etymology (e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/zelo#Spanish" title="wikt:zelo">
          zelo
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ziza%C3%B1a#Spanish" title="wikt:zizaña">
          zizaña
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ), but this usage was largely reduced during the 1860—1880s, so these words became
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/celo#Spanish" title="wikt:celo">
          celo
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ciza%C3%B1a#Spanish" title="wikt:cizaña">
          cizaña
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       . The letter ⟨x⟩ was replaced by ⟨j⟩ in 1815,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ort1815_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ort1815-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       although word-final ⟨x⟩ remained until 1832 (e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/relox#Spanish" title="wikt:relox">
          relox
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , now
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/reloj#Spanish" title="wikt:reloj">
          reloj
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ort1832_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ort1832-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The combinations ⟨je⟩ and ⟨ji⟩ were originally used only in a few etymological cases (e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Jes%C3%BAs#Spanish" title="wikt:Jesús">
          Jesús
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Jerem%C3%ADas#Spanish" title="wikt:Jeremías">
          Jeremías
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ) and also in diminutives (
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pajita#Spanish" title="wikt:pajita">
          pajita
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ); after the reform of 1815, ⟨xe⟩ and ⟨xi⟩ were replaced by ⟨ge⟩ and ⟨gi⟩ in the
       <i>
        Ortografía
       </i>
       but by ⟨je⟩ and ⟨ji⟩ in the
       <i>
        Diccionario
       </i>
       ; since 1832, the spelling was firmly established to be ⟨je⟩ and ⟨ji⟩. Also, unetymological spellings with ⟨ge⟩, ⟨gi⟩ (that is, words that did not have
       <i>
        g
       </i>
       in Latin) were changed to ⟨je⟩, ⟨ji⟩ (e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/muger#Spanish" title="wikt:muger">
          muger
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , from Latin
       <i>
        <span lang="la" xml:lang="la">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/mulier#Latin" title="wikt:mulier">
          mulier
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , became
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/mujer#Spanish" title="wikt:mujer">
          mujer
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       Old Spanish used to distinguish /s/ and /z/ between vowels, and it distinguished them by using ⟨ss⟩ for the former and ⟨s⟩ for the latter, e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/osso#Spanish" title="wikt:osso">
          osso
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ('bear') and
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/oso#Spanish" title="wikt:oso">
          oso
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ('I dare to'). In orthography, the distinction was suppressed in 1763.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ort1763_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ort1763-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Words spelled in modern Spanish with ⟨cua⟩, ⟨cuo⟩ (e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cuando#Spanish" title="wikt:cuando">
          cuando
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cuatro#Spanish" title="wikt:cuatro">
          cuatro
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cuota#Spanish" title="wikt:cuota">
          cuota
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ) were written with ⟨qua⟩, ⟨quo⟩ up until 1815.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ort1815_28-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ort1815-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1726, most double consonants were simplified (e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/grammatica#Spanish" title="wikt:grammatica">
          grammatica
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       →
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/gram%C3%A1tica#Spanish" title="wikt:gramática">
          gramática
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/addicion#Spanish" title="wikt:addicion">
          addicion
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       →
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/adici%C3%B3n#Spanish" title="wikt:adición">
          adición
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       )
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ort1726_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ort1726-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       —but the ⟨m⟩ of a prefix before the ⟨m⟩ of a root was differentiated to ⟨n⟩ in 1763 (e.g. "
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/commover#Spanish" title="wikt:commover">
          co
          <b>
           m
          </b>
          mover
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       →
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/conmover#Spanish" title="wikt:conmover">
          <i>
           co
           <b>
            n
           </b>
           mover
          </i>
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ort1763_30-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ort1763-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       And the Graeco-Latin digraphs ⟨ch⟩, ⟨ph⟩, ⟨(r)rh⟩ and ⟨th⟩ were reduced to ⟨c⟩, ⟨f⟩, ⟨(r)r⟩ and ⟨t⟩, respectively (e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/christiano#Spanish" title="wikt:christiano">
          christiano
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       →
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cristiano#Spanish" title="wikt:cristiano">
          cristiano
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/triumpho#Spanish" title="wikt:triumpho">
          triumpho
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       →
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/triunfo#Spanish" title="wikt:triunfo">
          triunfo
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/myrrha#Spanish" title="wikt:myrrha">
          myrrha
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       →
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/mirra#Spanish" title="wikt:mirra">
          mirra
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/theatro#Spanish" title="wikt:theatro">
          theatro
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       →
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/teatro#Spanish" title="wikt:teatro">
          teatro
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       From 1741
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ort1741_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ort1741-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       to 1815, the
       <a href="/wiki/Circumflex" title="Circumflex">
        circumflex
       </a>
       was used over vowels to indicate that preceding ⟨ch⟩ and ⟨x⟩ should be pronounced /k/ and /ks/ respectively and not /tʃ/ and /x/, e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ex%C3%A2ctitud#Spanish" title="wikt:exâctitud">
          exâctitud
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/patriarch%C3%A2#Spanish" title="wikt:patriarchâ">
          patriarchâ
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The use of accent marks in publishing varies with different historical periods, due mainly to reforms promulgated by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Academia_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Real Academia Española">
        Spanish Royal Academy
       </a>
       . For example, many of the words that are today standardly written with an accent mark appeared more often without it up until around 1880. These include words with final stress ending in
       <i>
        -n
       </i>
       (e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/capit%C3%A1n#Spanish" title="wikt:capitán">
          capitán
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/tambi%C3%A9n#Spanish" title="wikt:también">
          también
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/jard%C3%ADn#Spanish" title="wikt:jardín">
          jardín
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/acci%C3%B3n#Spanish" title="wikt:acción">
          acción
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/com%C3%BAn#Spanish" title="wikt:común">
          común
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       —but not future-tense verb forms like
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ser%C3%A1n#Spanish" title="wikt:serán">
          serán
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/tendr%C3%A1n#Spanish" title="wikt:tendrán">
          tendrán
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       );
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       verbs in the imperfect tense (e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ten%C3%ADa#Spanish" title="wikt:tenía">
          tenía
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/viv%C3%ADan#Spanish" title="wikt:vivían">
          vivían
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       );
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the possessives
       <i>
        mío
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        mía
       </i>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the word
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/d%C3%ADa#Spanish" title="wikt:día">
          día
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Meanwhile, one-letter words other than the conjunction
       <i>
        y
       </i>
       —namely the preposition
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       and the conjunctions
       <i>
        e
       </i>
       (the form of
       <i>
        y
       </i>
       before an [i] sound),
       <i>
        o
       </i>
       , and
       <i>
        u
       </i>
       (form of
       <i>
        o
       </i>
       before [o])—are generally written with accent marks from the mid-1700s to 1911.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The accent-marked infinitive
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/o%C3%ADr#Spanish" title="wikt:oír">
          oír
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       begins to outnumber the unaccented form around 1920.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Monosyllabic preterit verb forms such as
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/dio#Spanish" title="wikt:dio">
          dio
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fue#Spanish" title="wikt:fue">
          fue
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       were usually written with accent marks before the 1950s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The names of numbers in the upper teens and the twenties were originally written as three words (e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/diez#Spanish" title="wikt:diez">
          diez
         </a>
        </span>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/y#Spanish" title="wikt:y">
          y
         </a>
        </span>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/seis#Spanish" title="wikt:seis">
          seis
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/veinte#Spanish" title="wikt:veinte">
          veinte
         </a>
        </span>
        y
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/nueve#Spanish" title="wikt:nueve">
          nueve
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ), but nowadays they have come to be spelled predominantly as a single word (e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/diecis%C3%A9is#Spanish" title="wikt:dieciséis">
          dieciséis
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/veintinueve#Spanish" title="wikt:veintinueve">
          veintinueve
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ). For the numbers from 21 to 29, the "fused" forms emerged over the second half of the 19th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For those from 16 to 19, the one-word forms took the lead in the 1940s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Fusing of number-names above 30 (e.g.
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/treintaicinco#Spanish" title="wikt:treintaicinco">
          treintaicinco
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cuarentaiocho#Spanish" title="wikt:cuarentaiocho">
          cuarentaiocho
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       )
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is rare.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reform_proposals">
        Reform proposals
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_orthography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Reform proposals">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Bello_orthography" title="Bello orthography">
        Bello orthography
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In spite of the relatively regular orthography of Spanish, there have been several initiatives to
       <a href="/wiki/Spelling_reform" title="Spelling reform">
        simplify it further
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Bello" title="Andrés Bello">
        Andrés Bello
       </a>
       succeeded in making his proposal official in several South American countries, but they later returned to the standard set by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Academia_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Real Academia Española">
        Real Academia Española
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Another initiative, the Ortografia Fonetika Rasional Ispanoamerikana, remained a curiosity.
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Ram%C3%B3n_Jim%C3%A9nez" title="Juan Ramón Jiménez">
        Juan Ramón Jiménez
       </a>
       proposed changing ⟨ge⟩ and ⟨gi⟩ to ⟨je⟩ and ⟨ji⟩, but this is only applied in editions of his works or those of his wife,
       <a href="/wiki/Zenobia_Camprub%C3%AD" title="Zenobia Camprubí">
        Zenobia Camprubí
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Garc%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1rquez" title="Gabriel García Márquez">
        Gabriel García Márquez
       </a>
       raised the issue of reform during a congress at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zacatecas,_Zacatecas" title="Zacatecas, Zacatecas">
        Zacatecas
       </a>
       , most notoriously advocating for the suppression of ⟨h⟩, which is mute in Spanish, but, despite his prestige, no serious changes were adopted. The Academies, however, from time to time have made minor changes, such as allowing
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/este#Spanish" title="wikt:este">
          este
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       instead of
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%C3%A9ste#Spanish" title="wikt:éste">
          éste
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       ('this one'), when there is no possible confusion.
      </p>
      <p>
       A
       <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Spanish" title="Mexican Spanish">
        Mexican Spanish
       </a>
       convention is to spell certain indigenous words with ⟨x⟩ rather than the ⟨j⟩ that would be the standard spelling in Spanish. This is generally due to the origin of the word (or the present pronunciation) containing the
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiceless postalveolar fricative">
        voiceless postalveolar fricative
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʃ/
       </span>
       sound or another
       <a href="/wiki/Sibilant" title="Sibilant">
        sibilant
       </a>
       that is not used in modern standard Spanish. The most noticeable word with this feature is
       <i>
        México
       </i>
       (see
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toponymy_of_Mexico" title="Toponymy of Mexico">
        Toponymy of Mexico
       </a>
       ). The Real Academia Española recommends this spelling.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_United_States" title="Spanish language in the United States">
        American Spanish
       </a>
       colloquial term
       <i>
        chicano
       </i>
       is shortened from
       <i>
        mechicano
       </i>
       , which uses
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /tʃ/
       </span>
       in place of the
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʃ/
       </span>
       of rural Mexican Spanish
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /meʃiˈkano/
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Arabic_alphabet">
        Arabic alphabet
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_orthography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Arabic alphabet">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       In the 15th and 16th centuries, Spanish (as well as
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judeo-Spanish" title="Judeo-Spanish">
        Ladino
       </a>
       ) was sometimes written in the
       <a href="/wiki/Arabic_alphabet" title="Arabic alphabet">
        Arabic alphabet
       </a>
       by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moriscos" title="Moriscos">
        moriscos
       </a>
       . This form of Spanish is called
       <a href="/wiki/Aljamiado" title="Aljamiado">
        aljamiado
       </a>
       .
      </p>

          </i>
          <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
           No obstante, en el X Congreso de la Asociación de Academias de la Lengua Española, celebrado en 1994, se acordó adoptar para los diccionarios académicos, a petición de varios organismos internacionales, el orden alfabético latino universal, en el que la
          </span>
          ch
          <i>
           y la
          </i>
          ll
          <i>
           no se consideran letras independientes. En consecuencia, estas dos letras pasan a alfabetizarse en los lugares que les corresponden dentro de la C (entre -cg- y -ci-) y dentro de la L (entre -lk- y -lm-), respectivamente.
          </i>
         </span>
         "

           <span style="display:none;">
