        <li id="cite_note-Approximant-11">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-Approximant_11-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Approximant_11-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Approximant_11-2">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              c
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Approximant_11-3">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              d
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Approximant_11-4">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              e
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Approximant_11-5">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              f
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Approximant_11-6">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              g
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /b/
          </span>
          ,
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /d/
          </span>
          ,
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ʝ/
          </span>
          and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ɡ/
          </span>
          are
          <a href="/wiki/Approximant_consonant" title="Approximant consonant">
           approximants
          </a>
          (
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [β̞]
          </span>
          ,
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ð̞]
          </span>
          ,
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ʝ˕]
          </span>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ɣ˕]
          </span>
          ; represented here without the undertacks) in all places except after a pause, after an
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /n/
          </span>
          or
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /m/
          </span>
          , or—in the case of
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /d/
          </span>
          and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ʝ/
          </span>
          —after an
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /l/
          </span>
          , in which contexts they are stops
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [b, d, ɟʝ, ɡ]
          </span>
          , not dissimilar from English
          <i>
           b, d, j, g.
          </i>
          (
          <a href="#CITEREFMartínez-CeldránFernández-PlanasCarrera-Sabaté2003">
           Martínez-Celdrán, Fernández-Planas &amp; Carrera-Sabaté 2003
          </a>
          :257–8)
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-seseo-12">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-seseo_12-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-seseo_12-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-seseo_12-2">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              c
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          In Andalusia, Canary Islands, and Spanish America
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /θ/
          </span>
          has merged into
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /
           <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_fricative#Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiceless alveolar fricative">
            s
           </a>
           /
          </span>
          ; see
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seseo" title="Seseo">
           seseo
          </a>
          and
          <a href="#CITEREFMartínez-CeldránFernández-PlanasCarrera-Sabaté2003">
           Martínez-Celdrán, Fernández-Planas &amp; Carrera-Sabaté (2003
          </a>
          :258) for more information.
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-13">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-13">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          In a small number of borrowed words, such as Kir
          <b>
           ch
          </b>
          ner, this is
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [
           <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiceless postalveolar fricative">
            ʃ
           </a>
           ]
          </span>
          .
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-14">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-14">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          Modern words in which
          <i>
           h
          </i>
          is derived from Latin
          <i>
           f
          </i>
          (e.g.
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/hacer#Spanish" title="wikt:hacer">
             hacer
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          ,
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/hablar#Spanish" title="wikt:hablar">
             hablar
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          ) were spelled with
          <i>
           f
          </i>
          , pronounced
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [f]
          </span>
          , in
          <a href="/wiki/Old_Spanish_language" title="Old Spanish language">
           Old Spanish
          </a>
          (e.g.
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fazer#Spanish" title="wikt:fazer">
             fazer
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          ,
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fablar#Spanish" title="wikt:fablar">
             fablar
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          ), and there was a transitional stage pronounced
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [h]
          </span>
          before the sound was entirely lost; hence the modern spelling with
          <i>
           h
          </i>
          . But in words derived from Latin words with
          <i>
           h
          </i>
          (e.g.
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/hoy#Spanish" title="wikt:hoy">
             hoy
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          ,
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/prohibir#Spanish" title="wikt:prohibir">
             prohibir
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          ), the letter was always silent in Spanish. And words beginning with either of the diphthongs
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [je]
          </span>
          or
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [we]
          </span>
          (e.g.
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/hielo#Spanish" title="wikt:hielo">
             hielo
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          ,
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/huevo#Spanish" title="wikt:huevo">
             huevo
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          ) were given an initial
          <i>
           h
          </i>
          in spelling (always silent) to ensure that their initial
          <a href="/wiki/Semivowel" title="Semivowel">
           glide
          </a>
          was not read as a consonant (in Old Spanish, the letters
          <i>
           i
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           j
          </i>
          were often interchanged, as were
          <i>
           u
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           v
          </i>
          ).
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-spanish_w-15">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-spanish_w_15-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-spanish_w_15-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-spanish_w_15-2">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              c
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          Some speakers may pronounce word-initial
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [w]
          </span>
          with an
          <a href="/wiki/Epenthesis" title="Epenthesis">
           epenthetic
          </a>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ɡ/
          </span>
          , e.g.
          <i>
           H
           <b>
            u
           </b>
           ila
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈɡwila]~[ˈwila]
          </span>
          ,
          <i>
           h
           <b>
            u
           </b>
           eso
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈgweso]~[ˈweso]
          </span>
          ,
          <i>
           <b>
            w
           </b>
           aterpolo
          </i>
          [
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           ˈgwaterˈpolo
          </span>
          ] ~ [
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           ˈwaterˈpolo
          </span>
          ].
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-16">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-16">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          For most speakers, the ⟨j⟩ is silent at the end of a word, in which case
          <i>
           relo
           <b>
            j
           </b>
          </i>
          is pronounced
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [reˈlo]
          </span>
          .
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-nasal-17">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-nasal_17-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-nasal_17-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-nasal_17-2">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              c
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          The
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasal_stop" title="Nasal stop">
           nasal consonants
          </a>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /n, m, ɲ/
          </span>
          only contrast before vowels. Before consonants, they assimilate to the consonant's
          <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
           place of articulation
          </a>
          . This is partially reflected in the orthography: only ⟨m⟩ is written before ⟨b⟩ and ⟨p⟩; but only ⟨n⟩ is written before ⟨v⟩ (although the combination
          <i>
           nv
          </i>
          represents the same sounds as
          <i>
           mb
          </i>
          ) and ⟨f⟩. Word-finally, only
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /n/
          </span>
          occurs, normally spelled ⟨n⟩; but ⟨m⟩ is used in some loanwords.
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-18">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-18">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          In the verb
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/subrayar#Spanish" title="wikt:subrayar">
             subrayar
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          the trilled initial
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [r]
          </span>
          of the root
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/raya#Spanish" title="wikt:raya">
             raya
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          is maintained, even with the prefix
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/sub-#Spanish" title="wikt:sub-">
             sub-
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          . The same goes for
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ciudadreale%C3%B1o#Spanish" title="wikt:ciudadrealeño">
             ciudadrealeño
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          (from
          <i>
           Ciudad Real
          </i>
          ). However, after vowels, the initial ⟨r⟩ of the root becomes ⟨rr⟩ in prefixed or compound words:
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/prorrogar#Spanish" title="wikt:prorrogar">
             prorrogar
            </a>
           </span>
           ,
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/infrarrojo#Spanish" title="wikt:infrarrojo">
             infrarrojo
            </a>
           </span>
           ,
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/autorretrato#Spanish" title="wikt:autorretrato">
             autorretrato
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          .
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-debuccalize-19">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-debuccalize_19-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-debuccalize_19-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-debuccalize_19-2">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              c
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          For
          <a href="/wiki/Spanish_dialects_and_varieties#Variants_of_/s/_and_coda_/s/_debuccalization" title="Spanish dialects and varieties">
           many speakers
          </a>
          ,
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /s/
          </span>
          may
          <a href="/wiki/Debuccalization" title="Debuccalization">
           debuccalize
          </a>
          or
          <a href="/wiki/Elision" title="Elision">
           be deleted
          </a>
          in the
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syllable_coda" title="Syllable coda">
           syllable coda
          </a>
          (at the end of words and before consonants).
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-20">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-20">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          In words with the combination
          <i>
           -xs-
          </i>
          (e.g.,
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/exsenador#Spanish" title="wikt:exsenador">
             exsenador
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          ), the pronunciation is
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ks]
          </span>
          , and the two
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [
           <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_fricative#Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant" title="Voiceless alveolar fricative">
            s
           </a>
           ]
          </span>
          sounds are merged into one. The same goes for
          <i>
           -xc-
          </i>
          before
          <i>
           e, i
          </i>
          (e.g.,
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/excelente#Spanish" title="wikt:excelente">
             excelente
            </a>
           </span>
          </i>
          ) in varieties with
          <i>
           seseo
          </i>
          .
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-Semivowel-21">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-Semivowel_21-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          In Spanish, the letters
          <b>
           i
          </b>
          and
          <b>
           u
          </b>
          can combine with other vowels to form
          <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">
           diphthongs
          </a>
          (e.g.
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <i>
             c
             <b>
              i
             </b>
             elo
            </i>
           </span>
          </i>
          ,
          <i>
           <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
            <i>
             c
             <b>
              u
             </b>
             adro
            </i>
           </span>
          </i>
          ).
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-22">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-22">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#CITEREFButtBenjamin2011,_§39.2.2">
           Butt, Benjamin &amp; 2011, §39.2.2
          </a>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-23">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-23">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a class="external text" href="http://buscon.rae.es/dpdI/SrvltGUIBusDPD?lema=tilde2#7" rel="nofollow">
           7.
          </a>
          <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
           Acentuación de letras mayúsculas – Las letras mayúsculas, tanto si se trata de iniciales como si se integran en una palabra escrita enteramente en mayúsculas, deben llevar tilde si así les corresponde según las reglas de acentuación: Ángel, PROHIBIDO PISAR EL CÉSPED. No se acentúan, sin embargo, las mayúsculas que forman parte de las siglas (→ sigla, 5b).
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
